  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">

<div id="review_2320523096" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2320523096" />
    <a title="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus"><img alt="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588320656p2/78485297.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2320523096?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " href="/user/show/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus">Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus?shelf=pratchett-terry">pratchett-terry</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2320523096" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12135143606636538652">Some timid, rare Sci-Fi buds spring in the, unofficially second half, of the tour de force introduction into the settings of the Discworld, including multi dimensions, human sacrifice, possession, lynch mobs, and the apocalypse.<br/><br/>I do tend to ask myself how it would have been if Pratchett would have dealt with more sci-fi concepts instead of focusing on fantasy and society, and the whole multi dimension idea gives a tiny glimpse at what could have been. I´ll keep waiting for an author who might co</span>
  <span id="freeText12135143606636538652" style="display:none">Some timid, rare Sci-Fi buds spring in the, unofficially second half, of the tour de force introduction into the settings of the Discworld, including multi dimensions, human sacrifice, possession, lynch mobs, and the apocalypse.<br /><br />I do tend to ask myself how it would have been if Pratchett would have dealt with more sci-fi concepts instead of focusing on fantasy and society, and the whole multi dimension idea gives a tiny glimpse at what could have been. I´ll keep waiting for an author who might combine the stellar writing with cosmic ideas to form galactic novels of universal dimensions, but, realist that I am, I fear it might not be in my lifetime, if ever. Pratchett was an ingenious, exceptional phenomenon and possibly groups of writers could collaboratively create something close to it with the help of the audience and proofreaders participating in the process, but one woman/man alone? Forget it. <br /><br />There have been many variations of the unwilling, tentative, comedic hero, but someone like Rincewind has to be topped, as Pratchett is able to awake sympathy for a disagreeable, incompetent, and manipulative wanna be fringe pop wizard. One can´t get enough of seeing which terrible, earthshaking problem he might cause next without even recognizing.<br /><br />Magic can go so many ways and Pratchett doesn´t just make fun of the stereotypes, he gives some new, fresh ideas to the mix I can´t mention without spoilering and I am too lazy to copy and paste the <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> formatting template.<br /><br />And here comes the DEATH. I don´t know how many personifications of evanescence might have been inspired by this skinny buddy, but hardly someone came closer to demonstrate the importance of carpe diem than this human studying manifestation of the not so grim reaper with time management issues.<br /><br />World domination, ultimate power, and invincibility are as ridiculous as popular, but Pratchett gives the setting a new special taste by satirizing it with the allegedly mundane hurdles towards entity status that hide the key to the destruction of the maniac.<br /><br />Rincewind gets a bit insane in the membrane, although it´s difficult to see the difference, very alternative physics change some parts of the fictional reality, and after finishing, the reader is ready to enter the Discworld with more or less profound knowledge about why what is happening when. Just joking, reading Pratchett is never done in one sitting, next to the mandatory rereading passages to relaugh, the ideas keep rotating in ones´ mind, characters and scenes coming to life without even asking, as hardly seen or felt before after finishing other reads.<br /><br />It´s impressing how Pratchett managed to establish many of the settings and characters in the hero´s journey of his first two novels and the style of just showing some places, presenting the inhabitants, harvesting some laughs, planting McGuffins´and Chekhovs´for the further parts, and continuing the introduction trip without looking back is something modern fantasy is not used to anymore. Today there are more fast cuts between perspectives, always cliffhangery, well plotted, suspenseful, retrospectives,… in modern writing that is far less exhausting to read and difficult to follow than this classic series, one of the reasons some might find Pratchett hard to read. <br /><br />I don´t know if there are many people who may be able to find all the innuendos, connotations, and subtilities hidden in the Discworld, as one would have to have immense knowledge about so many different fields to fully enjoy each treasure hidden by this literary prodigy.<br /><br />Tropes show how literature is conceptualized and created and which mixture of elements makes works and genres unique: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Literature/TheLightFantastic">https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.ph...</a><br /><br />This one is added to all Pratchettian reviews:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scheibenwelt-Romane#Liste_der_Romane">https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scheibe...</a> <br />The idea of the dissected motifs rocks, highlighting the main real world inspirational elements of fiction and satire is something usually done with so called higher literature, but a much more interesting field in readable literature, as it offers the joy of reading, subtle criticism, and feeling smart all together.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12135143606636538652" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1106150664" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1106150664" />
    <a title="Lyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn"><img alt="Lyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495541962p2/5253785.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1106150664?book_show_action=true">Nov 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyn" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn">Lyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1106150664" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2870624245963969818">Reading Sir Terry Pratchett’s Discworld series makes me smile. Because of his writing I invented the "Smile-O-meter" which measures smiles per book. Pratchett always scores high.<br/><br/>Three years after Terry Pratchett published <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34497.The_Color_of_Magic__Discworld___1__Rincewind___1_' title='The Color of Magic (Discworld, #1; Rincewind, #1) by Terry Pratchett' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Color of Magic</a>, the first Discworld book, he published the second, The Light Fantastic, having decided convincingly that this was a worthwhile project.<br/><br/>Though the action in The Light Fantastic takes over immediately following the events in the first book, Rincewind has falle</span>
  <span id="freeText2870624245963969818" style="display:none">Reading Sir Terry Pratchett’s Discworld series makes me smile. Because of his writing I invented the "Smile-O-meter" which measures smiles per book. Pratchett always scores high.<br><br>Three years after Terry Pratchett published <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34497.The_Color_of_Magic__Discworld___1__Rincewind___1_" title="The Color of Magic (Discworld, #1; Rincewind, #1) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">The Color of Magic</a>, the first Discworld book, he published the second, The Light Fantastic, having decided convincingly that this was a worthwhile project.<br><br>Though the action in The Light Fantastic takes over immediately following the events in the first book, Rincewind has fallen off of the edge of the world, this novel seems to gather momentum from a good but somewhat shaky start and proceed with a comic authority. While The Colour of Magic could have been a funny stand alone, Pratchett’s entry with The Light Fantastic seems to usher in a certainty that the Discworld as a multiverse, as a literary institution, has begun and with no end in sight.<br><br>Actually, I suppose he could have written a third, making the obligatory trilogy and then moving on to something else, but Pratchett wraps up his story tidily and leaves the fertile soil of Discworld as a fun idea from which more books can be written. (There are over 50 works in publication, and the series is a phenomenon with over 80 million novels sold and in 37 languages. Pratchett himself was knighted in 2009).<br><br>So what is all the fuss about? Our heroes Rincewind and Twoflower go on an adventure to save the world, or try to, or accidentally end up in all the right places, or something. <br><br>The real hero of the novel, and of the series, is Pratchett himself. It is his narration that amuses, cajoles, and encourages laughter and that keeps the reader’s attention. Playfully, and with wry English humor, Pratchett weaves a fun fantasy story with references to Biblical, classical, and mythical themes as well as modern subjects like Conan the Barbarian.<br><br>It is simply, a lot of fun. And produces smiles.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1517070914i/24946605._SY540_.jpg" width="247" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="2870624245963969818" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback " href="/book/show/601239.The_Light_Fantastic">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22809267-adrian?shelf=fantasy-and-magic">fantasy-and-magic</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2468667998" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer833601233022400640">Review to follow tomorrow, but tell me why have I waited so long to re-read the Discworld books. 😢😳<br/><br/>And the honest answer is, well for a while I didn't have a copy of any Discworld novel, due to the fact that (as I think I've mentioned before (oh no am I getting so old I'm repeating myself ?) ) I lost so so so many books in one of my house moves, Discworld novels amongst them. And then somehow I forgot just how good the books were.<br/><br/>So The Light Fantastic picks up where The Colour of Magic left off</span>
  <span id="freeText833601233022400640" style="display:none">Review to follow tomorrow, but tell me why have I waited so long to re-read the Discworld books. 😢😳<br /><br />And the honest answer is, well for a while I didn't have a copy of any Discworld novel, due to the fact that (as I think I've mentioned before (oh no am I getting so old I'm repeating myself ?) ) I lost so so so many books in one of my house moves, Discworld novels amongst them. And then somehow I forgot just how good the books were.<br /><br />So The Light Fantastic picks up where The Colour of Magic left off and we find Rincwind, Twoflower and the Luggage in a precarious (as normal) situation. In my view this is better than Colour of Magic in that it is less a series of quite disjointed stories and more a whole novel. We meet various other characters that help/hinder/attack/welcome our intrepid trio as well as separating them and ultimately bringing it all back together for an amazing finale. A great book that showcases the amazing talent that Terry Pratchett had . <br />A more than solid 5 star read and already a favourite of 2019.</span>

<div id="review_571288331" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/571288331" />
    <a title="Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley"><img alt="Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508811508p2/4213258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/571288331?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer571288331" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15056334514960411351">Re-read with buddies!<br/><br/>I'm still very much enjoying these early Pratchett books, especially in mind that I'll be seeing a *lot* more of these folks in the near future. And even if I'll mainly be focused on folks I haven't seen yet, anyway, I'm still enjoying what may as well be an overview primer of the whole Discworld universe.<br/><br/>That being said, I think Rincewind is given a bad rap in the series. I love the hell out of him. He's the ultimate bumbling idiot under the geas of a penultimate Eighth Spe</span>
  <span id="freeText15056334514960411351" style="display:none">Re-read with buddies!<br /><br />I'm still very much enjoying these early Pratchett books, especially in mind that I'll be seeing a *lot* more of these folks in the near future. And even if I'll mainly be focused on folks I haven't seen yet, anyway, I'm still enjoying what may as well be an overview primer of the whole Discworld universe.<br /><br />That being said, I think Rincewind is given a bad rap in the series. I love the hell out of him. He's the ultimate bumbling idiot under the geas of a penultimate Eighth Spell, the casting of which will make or destroy the universe or something, and the making and breaking is ultimately left up only to him.<br /><br />And he's a wizard with a hat that says "wizzard" on it. You know... to make sure people understand that he's actually one of their kind. :) I particularly loved the bits with the floating rocks and the computers of the universe and the dungeon universes and, of course, Cohen the Barbarian.<br /><br />It's funny, it's BIG, and we even get to see the tourism industry take off in a really big way, even going so far as to have the very first tourist play a big part in a very special birth. Aww<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www">www</a>... So sweet! :)<br /><br />Plotwise, I think it's well up to the standards of the rest of the series and while Rincewind falls away in people's favor, *cry* He'll always have a very special place in my heart.<br /><br />And by the way, that sword is definitely smarter than him. Oh well! <br /><br />Great fun! Even better the second time!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15056334514960411351" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15969648530164824456">I adore Terry Pratchett. I don't know how to elaborate on that so I'll just share some of my favorite moments in Light Fantastic.<br/><br/>Snarky social commentary:<br/><i>
  <blockquote>She is there, down below the mines and sea ooze and fake fossil bones put there by a Creator with nothing better to do than upset archaeologists and give them silly ideas.</blockquote>
  <blockquote>Not for the first time she reflected that there were many drawbacks to being a swordswoman, not the least of which was that men didn't take you seriously until you'd act</blockquote></i></span>
  <span id="freeText15969648530164824456" style="display:none">I adore Terry Pratchett. I don't know how to elaborate on that so I'll just share some of my favorite moments in Light Fantastic.<br /><br />Snarky social commentary:<br /><i>
  <blockquote>She is there, down below the mines and sea ooze and fake fossil bones put there by a Creator with nothing better to do than upset archaeologists and give them silly ideas.</blockquote>
  <blockquote>Not for the first time she reflected that there were many drawbacks to being a swordswoman, not the least of which was that men didn't take you seriously until you'd actually killed them, by which time it didn't really matter anyway. (...) But she was too big to be a thief, too honest to be an assassin, too intelligent to be a wife, and too proud to enter the only other female profession generally available.</blockquote>
</i><br />General humor: <br /><i>
  <blockquote>Someone who spent his life living rough under the sky knew the value of a good thick book, which ought to outlast at least a season of cooking fires if you were careful how you tore the pages out.</blockquote>
  <blockquote> Magic! So that's what it felt like! No wonder wizards didn't have much truck with sex!</blockquote>
  <blockquote>"She's not bad," said Twoflower. "She's going to marry a friend of ours."<br />"Does he know?"</blockquote>
  <blockquote>Most people on the Disc were currently in a state of mind normally achievable only by a lifetime of dedicated meditation or about thirty seconds of illegal herbage.</blockquote>
</i><br />The lamest pun ever:<br /><i>
  <blockquote>"Rincewind, all the shops have been smashed open, there was a whole bunch of people across the street helping themselves to musical instruments, can you believe that?"<br />"Yeah," said Rincewind. "Luters, I expect."</blockquote>
</i><br />The Luggage remains my favorite:<br /><i>
  <blockquote>The Luggage said nothing.<br />"Look he's not my responsibility," said Rincewind. "Let's be absolutely clear about that."<br />The Luggage said nothing, but louder this time.</blockquote>
  <blockquote>"Um," said Twoflower. "Yes. That's about enough, I think. Put him down, please."<br />The Luggage gave a creak of betrayal at the sound of its master's voice.</blockquote>
</i><br />I might briefly have shipped Rincewind and Twoflower in this moment:<br /><i>
  <blockquote>(Rincewind, about Twoflower) He just looks at things, but nothing he looks at is ever the same again. Including me, I expect.</blockquote>
</i><br /></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_28987832" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/28987832" />
    <a title="Jamie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1385106-jamie"><img alt="Jamie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1217535570p2/1385106.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/28987832?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jamie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jamie" href="/user/show/1385106-jamie">Jamie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer28987832" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9570286643948594492">I'm pretty sure people have told me about Pratchett and his Diskworld series before, usually working in the phrase "He's the Douglas Adams of fantasy" into the description. But the problem was that I always felt that I had had enough of Adams after the third Hithiker's Guide to the Galaxy book, and whenever I scanned Pratchett's section in the bookstore I was immediately put off by not knowing where to start reading among the approximately five hundred thousand Diskworld books. I'm glad I finall</span>
  <span id="freeText9570286643948594492" style="display:none">I'm pretty sure people have told me about Pratchett and his Diskworld series before, usually working in the phrase "He's the Douglas Adams of fantasy" into the description. But the problem was that I always felt that I had had enough of Adams after the third Hithiker's Guide to the Galaxy book, and whenever I scanned Pratchett's section in the bookstore I was immediately put off by not knowing where to start reading among the approximately five hundred thousand Diskworld books. I'm glad I finally took the time to find out that these two books, The Colour of Magic and The Light Fantastic, jointly comprise the first tale in the series, and that they were definitely worth reading.<br /><br />The Diskworld books are essentially satire of the high fantasy genre, or at least that's the foundation upon which everything else is built. This pair of books follows the misadventures of Rincewind, a utterly inept and thoroughly cowardly wizard, and Twoflowers, a clueless traveler who happens to be in possession of both endless optimism and a magical suitcase that's always wandering off and messily devouring people who get in its way. Things go from bad to worse for the two as divine powers both deliver them into and yank them out of all kinds of fantastic perils.<br /><br />As someone who grew up reading plenty of this kind of thing and playing a lot of Dungeons&amp; Dragons, I'm familiar enough with the genre and trappings that Pratchett lampoons. Yes, there's the Conan parody, there's the Dragonriders of Pern tribute, there's the in-joke about Leiber's Fafhrd and Gray Mouser. But that's easy. The thing that made me almost immediately fall in love with these books is the author's dry wit and his ability to derive humor not only from the absurdity of the story (and believe me, it gets plenty absurd) but also from just good old fashioned turns of phrase, wry commentary, and jokes. The guy just has an amazing ability to stuff five or six jokes into a single sentence, most of them making masterful use of that trusty standby of British humor, irony. It's really smart and really funny, and the fact that it builds on the inherent silliness of the high fantasy genre is just icing.<br /><br />I should also note how imaginative Pratchett is, which is a useful quality given his subject matter. He bounces his heroes from one (generally horrible and dangerous) situation to another at a frantic pace, and his ability to come up with new material and new situations amazes me. And while many of them are obvious parodies of fantasy staples, just as many seem to be wholly new creations. As one small (and obligatory) example, the Diskworld itself is a flat coin of a world that rides atop four enormous elephants, who themselves ride on the back of a colossal turtle with two continent-sized flippers that it uses to swim slowly through the cold reaches of space.<br /><br />But at the same time, if I have one complaint about these first two books, it's that they're almost maniacal in their plotting. While it's nice to see Pratchett's considerable imagination and humor on display as we go from situation to situation, the first book reads like an extended doodle with little plot and a whole "gods playing games with mortals" subtext that's entirely dropped in the next book. There's also one Conan the Barbarian parody that's abruptly dropped in favor of another Conan the Barbarian parody who Pratchett apparently liked better. It's not until the latter part of the second book does an overall plot come into play, but honestly I was enjoying myself so much I really didn't mind. Expect to see lots more Discworld books reviewed here in the future. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9570286643948594492" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  <span id="freeText3944603535037586576" style="display:none"><i>"You still love Terry Pratchett, after all these years?"<br>"Always."</i><br>- Gandalf, Return of the Jedi.<br><br>Jokes aside, <b>my teen years were marked by edginess, heavy metal, nihilism and Terry Pratchett.</b> I think the latter was never a phase; he is an author that will always be in my heart and in my head, <b>providing bellyache-inducing laughs whenever Death has an identity crisis</b> (which is always) or when <b>Nanny Ogg is trying to explain to her seemingly infinite children who their real fathers are</b>(and lying through her teeth).<br><br>Even though Rincewind and Twoflower aren't my favourites, <b>they still hold a special place in my heart because they were in the first Pratchett books I read.</b><br><br><i>courtesy of Jen's mini review</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1559063422i/27584707._SX540_.jpg" alt="Image result for rincewind and twoflower fanart" width="304" height="245" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_1384357085" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1384357085" />
    <a title="Evelyn (devours and digests words)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words"><img alt="Evelyn (devours and digests words)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556809829p2/38658747.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1384357085?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evelyn (devours and digests words)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evelyn (devours and digests words)" href="/user/show/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words">Evelyn (devours and digests words)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11186726-the-light-fantastic">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=a-touch-of-satire">a-touch-of-satire</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=fantastical">fantastical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=writing-i-would-love-to-imitate">writing-i-would-love-to-imitate</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=bagful-of-laughs">bagful-of-laughs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=unique-story-lines">unique-story-lines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=fey-folks">fey-folks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=cover-beauts">cover-beauts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38658747-evelyn-devours-and-digests-words?shelf=shocking">shocking</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1384357085" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14587922848853304493"><i>"Inside every sane person, there's a madman struggling to get out. That's what I've always thought. No one goes mad quicker than a totally sane person." </i><br/><br/><b>The second installment in the Discworld series is a bigger, funnier delight. One heck of a Laugh Out Loud read.</b><br/><br/>Something I consider very special in Sir Terry Pratchett's works is that many authors can pull off a joke every once in a while in their stories but <b>Mr Pratchett managed to keep the whole thing comical, while at the time <i>satirical.</i></b> Not </span>
  <span id="freeText14587922848853304493" style="display:none"><i>"Inside every sane person, there's a madman struggling to get out. That's what I've always thought. No one goes mad quicker than a totally sane person." </i><br /><br /><b>The second installment in the Discworld series is a bigger, funnier delight. One heck of a Laugh Out Loud read.</b><br /><br />Something I consider very special in Sir Terry Pratchett's works is that many authors can pull off a joke every once in a while in their stories but <b>Mr Pratchett managed to keep the whole thing comical, while at the time <i>satirical.</i></b> Not once did I not grin or snort out loud.<br /><br />In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/833512.The_Colour_of_Magic_The_Illustrated_Screenplay" title="The Colour of Magic The Illustrated Screenplay by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Colour of Magic</a>, Rincewind was last seen (read?) falling off the rim of the world. Well, he landed safely on his arse. Thank goodness or he couldn't be much use if he's dead.<br /><br />Things are turning quite grim now. Great A'Tuin the turtle is wading its giant flippers toward a 'red star'. The closer it is (I feel very sorry for calling the World Turtle an 'it' but in my defense, 'it's' sex is still undetermined afterall!) to the star, the weaker and more unbalanced the magic is back in Discworld!<br /><br />The only way to prevent the apocalypse is to recite all 8 spells from a magic book called Octavo. However one last spell is missing. Where could it be?! It also didn't help Rincewind's situation and mood when he found out that there's a certain prophecy about him.<br /><br />I'm not a big reader when it comes to books with apocalypse in it looming just around the corner. Too bleak, I say. But this was a purely fun ride that follows with Rincewind's unfortunate adventures.<br /><br />The worldbuilding is still just as bizarre as the last book. Except now it has a fairytale feel to it. There's even a scene where Rincewind and Twoflower took refuge in a gingerbread house! Sounds familiar? *cough* Hansel and Gretel! *cough*<br /><br /><b>Characterizations [humans, fantastical creatures and things alike]: </b><br /><br />I have a very special place in my heart for nearly all the people <s>and creatures</s> in the book. Of course I have certain favourites myself but I couldn't resist liking nearly everything and everyone. It sounds so corny of me, I know. But damn it, I can't help myself not when they're all so fleshed out well. Definitely not when they each have their own unique quirky personality.<br /><br />Rincewind shows even more of his cynicism and it didn't exactly help his ill bedside manners being partnered with the impossibly, insufferably optimistic Twoflower.<br /><blockquote><br />"I expect everything will turn out quite all right in the end," said Twoflower.<br /><br />Rincewind looked at him. Remarks like that always threw him off.<br /><br />"Do you really believe that? I mean," he said. "Really?"<br /><br />"Well, things generally do work out satisfactorily, when you come to think about it."<br /><br />"If you think the total disruption of my life in the last year is satisfactory then you might be right. I've lost count of the times I've nearly been killed--"<br /><br />"Twenty-seven," said Twoflower.<br /><br /><i>"What?"</i> </blockquote><br /><br />He held a great disdain within him toward people and situations in life. He's not just <b>cynical</b>, I like to think of him as <b>pessimistic</b> too. He also has a knack of running in the opposite directions from things he's terrified of instead of plunging straight into the fire and save the day. Some people would say that he's quite the <b>coward</b>. I would say that he's quite the <b>survivalist.</b><br /><br /><blockquote>'He always held that panic was the best means of survival; back in the olden days, his theory went, people faced with hungry saber-toothed tigers could be divided very simply into those who panicked and those who stood there saying. "What a magnificent brute!" and "Here, pussy." </blockquote><br /><br />Rincewind's snappy moods, impatience and crankiness have really grown on me. Irregardless of how distasteful his actions may be at times!<br /><br />I have to tip my hat on behalf of Twoflower, the first tourist of Ankh-Morpork may be the only one who can understand and tolerate Rincewind. While he is pessimistic, <b>Twoflower is optimistic.</b> Rincewind's cowardly but Twoflowers's <b>noble and is willing to sacrifice himself to save others.</b> Rincewind is quick to rage but Twoflower's best merits are his patience and his forgiving nature.<br /><br /><blockquote>"Against the whole of human experience Twoflower believed that if only people would talk to each other, have a few drinks, exchange pictures of their grandchildren, maybe take in a show or something, then everything could be sorted out. He also believed that people were basically good but sometimes had their bad days."</blockquote><br /><br />How can I not resist someone like him? I can't!<b> He's so good-hearted, it either made you despise how he's so insufferably annoying at that or... you find him irresistible.</b> It is the latter for me.<br /><br />Then there's<b> The Luggage</b>, it's name suggest<i> what</i> it is. A luggage that carries laundries for its master! Except it's no ordinary luggage. For one thing, it has hundreds of tiny little legs to take it anywhere. It's lid serves as a mouth and when it wants to look menancing, it snaps the lid up and down. <b>Don't get too close - it's a luggage that bites and snaps <s>and eats people up!</s></b><br /><br />With the Luggage in your possession, you can be in no harm as long as:<br /><br /><blockquote>a) you're not trying to harm it's master and his friends.<br />b) you don't kick its wooden sides and be a big bully.<br />c) you don't try to force open its lid apart to see what treasure is inside (there are usually none).</blockquote><br /><br />So aside from looking menancing, what else does it do? You'd be awed that not only The Luggage is useful in carrying loads,<b> it is also very loyal, quick in thinking and even quicker so in taking actions</b> (with those hundreds of little legs? No doubt)<b> to save those in distress</b>. Don't ask me how a luggage can think. I have no idea! Point is, the Luggage can be real scary to the point that even barbarians soil their trousers. You should be scared.<br /><br />Then there are the minor people, creatures and things alike such as a group of incompetent swordsmen led by a woman, talking trees, a goblin, an imp who paints, a barbarian, DEATH and his comrades, stone trolls, a cursed shopkeeper, a mob of crazy superstitious people with pitchforks.... and so on and so forth. I expected to get clogged up with all these many minor characters coming and going. But not-so-surprisingly, I didn't feel confused or got side tracked by them. Each one of them has personalities and they're not forgettable. Not when they do or say something incredibly incredible, funny or stupid.<b> Pratchett can write about the smallest pebble on a ground of dirt and still make it interesting and full of persona.</b><br /><br />As a final conclusion, I can't say much except that... well, <b>this book</b> was just fucking fantastic and it <b>won my heart and soul completely</b>. That about sums up my thoughts. <br /><br />Besides, it's almost impossible to pick apart or find anything wrong in something that can switch on your 'HAHA' button each seconds. <i>The jokes are distracting!</i><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Doctor's Prescription and Warning:</u>
</b><br /><br />This is the medicine for when you feel blue or angry.<br /><br />No, it's not supposed to be some pills.<br /><br />It's<i> this</i> book.<br /><br />However, read with care for each sentences and every passages are induced with high dosages of humour. Limit your level of intake in case you overdosed on the words and choke on your spit bellowing with laughter.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14587922848853304493" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Gary " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27528763-gary"><img alt="Gary " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499717454p2/27528763.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/928714938?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gary " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gary " href="/user/show/27528763-gary">Gary </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27528763-gary?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27528763-gary?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer928714938" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9472058045166628564">This book was every bit as fun as the last- maybe more so. Since this is number two in series order, I am getting a feel for where the author was at the point in time it was written. The character development seems more vivid. Rincewind, the Luggage, the Druid sacrifice girl, and the over the hill barbarian fighter are characters that will live with me long after this series is done.<br/>This story has more of a quest feel to it than the last one did. It definitely builds to a strong climax. In order</span>
  <span id="freeText9472058045166628564" style="display:none">This book was every bit as fun as the last- maybe more so. Since this is number two in series order, I am getting a feel for where the author was at the point in time it was written. The character development seems more vivid. Rincewind, the Luggage, the Druid sacrifice girl, and the over the hill barbarian fighter are characters that will live with me long after this series is done.<br />This story has more of a quest feel to it than the last one did. It definitely builds to a strong climax. In order to avert certain doom, all of the eight great spells must be read in order. The eighth and final spell is, of course, in Rincewind’s mind. His death would solve that problem for the planet’s most powerful spell casters. <br /> The story progresses through one mishap after another as the author continues to add characters and build his world. Rather than read these books by order of character type (for example, all of the Rincewind stories followed by all of the Witches stories and so forth), I have chosen to attempt to read them chronologically. I think it gives a clear picture of where the author is at in a point in time and what his conception of this world and these characters is and is becoming.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9472058045166628564" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1371276832" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1371276832" />
    <a title="Tim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17042835-tim"><img alt="Tim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486434279p2/17042835.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1371276832?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tim" href="/user/show/17042835-tim">Tim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1371276832" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18292680612259192818">Another excellent Discworld adventure from the late Sir Pratchett. All that was missing in my judgement was more inspiration and positivity by the main characters 6 of 10 stars</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_2015685960" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2015685960" />
    <a title="Trish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3461034-trish"><img alt="Trish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588663568p2/3461034.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2015685960?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trish" href="/user/show/3461034-trish">Trish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback " href="/book/show/601239.The_Light_Fantastic">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2015685960" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16915704839039420778"><b>3.5 stars</b> (yes, I actually liked the first one a bit better)<br/><br/><i>"The important thing about having lots of things to remember is that you've got to go somewhere afterward where you can remember them, you see? You've got to stop. You haven't really been anywhere until you've got back home."</i><br/><br/>Thus, this second book in the Discworld series is about the continued adventure of Twoflower, the very first tourist, and Rincewind, the failed wiz(z)ard with only one spell in his head.<br/>We get to know more about tha</span>
  <span id="freeText16915704839039420778" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars</b> (yes, I actually liked the first one a bit better)<br><br><i>"The important thing about having lots of things to remember is that you've got to go somewhere afterward where you can remember them, you see? You've got to stop. You haven't really been anywhere until you've got back home."</i><br><br>Thus, this second book in the Discworld series is about the continued adventure of Twoflower, the very first tourist, and Rincewind, the failed wiz(z)ard with only one spell in his head.<br>We get to know more about that spell in particular and how it caused Rincewind to fail at being a wizard. Moreover, we get to see much more of the Unseen University and their machinations.<br>At the beginning, we start where the last novel ended and I really think the two books should be considered one story. Twoflower in the ship and Rincewind and the Luggage without a mode of transportation have "gone overboard". However, the most magical book on the entire Dicworld (the Octavo) can't let Rincewind die so magic saves them.<br>From there, they continue their journey through odd landscapes (a very peculiar forest for example) and meet new people (like Cohen, a parody of Conan the Barbarian).<br>Oh, and to make matters more interesting, we then find out that the Discworld is about to be destroyed unless the eight spells of the Octavo are being recited in time. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[What happens after they have been recited was actually one of my favourite scenes in the movie and this book - I mean BABY TURTLES! *swoons*<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1496523885i/22923442.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>What I also liked was the portrayal of DEATH's domain (not to mention <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[his adopted daughter - BWAHAHAHAHAHA <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>)! But then again, I always had a weakness for the bony fella. ;)<br><br>Again, the book had some interesting spins on ideas, witty observations about <s>our</s> the Discworld, as well as funny moments, but nothing groundbreaking or laugh-out-loud. As I stated before, I think this and the first should be regarded as one piece, because of the story and because of how it was delivered so it's no surprise there isn't much more to say about this except for what has already been said in my review for the previous volume.<br>However, I will point out that one of the saviors in this story and a wonderful character all on its own, was luggage! I really liked the little guy with his right-action-at-the-right-time interventions and "comments" on certain matters.<br><br>I marked a few lines and passages in this book again but am leaving you with this, one of my favourites:<br><i>"Inside every sane person there's a madman struggling to get out. That's what I've always thought. No one goes mad quicker than a totally sane person."</i></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="16915704839039420778" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_963753962" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/963753962" />
    <a title="Rob" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10743961-rob"><img alt="Rob" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422270416p2/10743961.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/963753962?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rob" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rob" href="/user/show/10743961-rob">Rob</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6457620-the-light-fantastic">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=author-male">author-male</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=humor">humor</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer963753962" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7250529456809206799"><b>Executive Summary:</b> I enjoyed this one a lot more than <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34497.The_Color_of_Magic__Discworld___1__Rincewind__1_' title='The Color of Magic (Discworld, #1; Rincewind #1) by Terry Pratchett' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Color of Magic</a>, and it made me glad I read that book first rather than starting with one of the later in the series.<br/><br/><b>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</b><br/>A moment of silence for the passing of a great man.<br/><br/><br/><br/>It's a shame it took the passing of Terry Pratchett for me to give this series a second chance. I've had numerous people tell me how much I'd like it. It was recommended again to me when I said I was in a funk and wanted something light and fun just a few days</span>
  <span id="freeText7250529456809206799" style="display:none"><b>Executive Summary:</b> I enjoyed this one a lot more than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34497.The_Color_of_Magic__Discworld___1__Rincewind__1_" title="The Color of Magic (Discworld, #1; Rincewind #1) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">The Color of Magic</a>, and it made me glad I read that book first rather than starting with one of the later in the series.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</b><br />A moment of silence for the passing of a great man.<br /><br /><br /><br />It's a shame it took the passing of Terry Pratchett for me to give this series a second chance. I've had numerous people tell me how much I'd like it. It was recommended again to me when I said I was in a funk and wanted something light and fun just a few days before his passing. <br /><br />I just wasn't sure about it though. I'm often stubborn. I know it. I like to read things in publication order. I know this series is more like a loose collection of stories set in the same world, but I still want to read it in the order it came out. So I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34497.The_Color_of_Magic__Discworld___1__Rincewind__1_" title="The Color of Magic (Discworld, #1; Rincewind #1) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">The Color of Magic</a> last year, and it was alright.<br /><br />I did plan on reading this book at some point, but I kept putting it off. I wish I hadn't. The humor was better, the plot was more interesting, and some great new characters were introduced.<br /><br />And the puns. Man there are some great puns in here. I had to stop reading for a few minutes because I was laughing so hard. I'm not normally big on puns, but they really worked for me in this book. I won't ruin them for you though, you should read them for yourself.<br /><br />So now I'm hooked on the series. I jumped right into <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34507.Equal_Rites__Discworld___3__Witches__1_" title="Equal Rites (Discworld, #3; Witches #1) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Equal Rites</a> and I'm nearly done with that. I'll likely be jumping right into <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/386372.Mort__Discworld___4__Death___1_" title="Mort (Discworld, #4; Death, #1) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Mort</a> after that.<br /><br />I'm sad Mr. Pratchett has left us, and that I didn't get a chance to meet him and thank him for his great work. But I'm excited by the fact that I have nearly 40 more books to enjoy. I may have to pace myself though as there will sadly only be one more to come.<br /><br />I can't say you should be stubborn like I am, and read in publication order. Most people seem to recommend starting with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/64216.Guards__Guards___Discworld___8__City_Watch__1_" title="Guards! Guards! (Discworld, #8; City Watch #1) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Guards! Guards!</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34484.Small_Gods__Discworld___13_" title="Small Gods (Discworld, #13) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Small Gods</a>. I will say that if you do start with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34497.The_Color_of_Magic__Discworld___1__Rincewind__1_" title="The Color of Magic (Discworld, #1; Rincewind #1) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">The Color of Magic</a> make sure you read this one too, because not only is it a continuation of the plot, it's a vast improvement in every way.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7250529456809206799" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1259301812" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1259301812" />
    <a title="Lindsay" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10326608-lindsay"><img alt="Lindsay" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588746288p2/10326608.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1259301812?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lindsay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindsay" href="/user/show/10326608-lindsay">Lindsay</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1259301812" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9415446086337248156">The story picks up where the first one left off, with Rincewind, Twoflower and the Luggage in dire peril. They're mysteriously saved and plonked down in the middle of a magical forest. Meanwhile an ominous red star has appeared in the sky of the disk and it appears to be growing each night. The Wizards of Unseen University want to read the Octavo to save the Disc, but Rincewind still has one of the Eight spells stuck in his head, so the hunt for the wizard is on.<br/><br/>I have no idea how many times I'v</span>
  <span id="freeText9415446086337248156" style="display:none">The story picks up where the first one left off, with Rincewind, Twoflower and the Luggage in dire peril. They're mysteriously saved and plonked down in the middle of a magical forest. Meanwhile an ominous red star has appeared in the sky of the disk and it appears to be growing each night. The Wizards of Unseen University want to read the Octavo to save the Disc, but Rincewind still has one of the Eight spells stuck in his head, so the hunt for the wizard is on.<br /><br />I have no idea how many times I've read this, other than I'm sure this is at least my third time through. I had set my expectations of these first few Discworld novels based on a memory that they weren't all that good compared to later novels in the series, but to my happy surprise I found myself greatly enjoying this. This novel in a lot of ways, rather than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/601238.The_Colour_of_Magic__Discworld___1_" title="The Colour of Magic (Discworld, #1) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">The Colour of Magic</a>, feels like the genesis of what the Discworld becomes.<br /><br />In this one you get the introduction of the Librarian, Death's daughter Ysabell, Cohen the Barbarian and the beginnings of the more nuanced character of Death himself. This quote from Death regarding the rampant stupidity of the Star cultists could easily have come from a much later book:<blockquote>NOT LIKE THIS. THE DEATH OF THE WARRIOR OR THE OLD MAN OR THE LITTLE CHILD, THIS I UNDERSTAND, AND I TAKE AWAY THE PAIN AND END THE SUFFERING. I DO NOT UNDERSTAND THIS DEATH-OF-THE-MIND.</blockquote>All-in-all, it's the first inklings of the strong character work, social commentary and razor sharp humor that have made Pratchett a household name.<br /><br />Very glad to revise my rating of this book to 5 stars and now I've very much looking forward to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34507.Equal_Rites__Discworld___3__Witches__1_" title="Equal Rites (Discworld, #3; Witches #1) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Equal Rites</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34499.Sourcery__Discworld___5__Rincewind__3_" title="Sourcery (Discworld, #5; Rincewind #3) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Sourcery</a>, neither of which I've reread before.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9415446086337248156" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1653247624" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1653247624" />
    <a title="RJ from the LBC" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/131730-rj-from-the-lbc"><img alt="RJ from the LBC" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605827139p2/131730.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1653247624?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="RJ from the LBC" class="user" itemprop="url" name="RJ from the LBC" href="/user/show/131730-rj-from-the-lbc">RJ from the LBC</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780062225689" href="/book/show/15818475-the-light-fantastic">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/131730-rj-from-the-lbc?shelf=guardian-1000-read">guardian-1000-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/131730-rj-from-the-lbc?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1653247624" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15933844685800043322">Laurel and Hardy. Riggs and Murtaugh. Oscar and Felix. And continuing the grand tradition, the Discworld's own Rincewind and Twoflower. This time the story centers around the Octavo and the 8th spell lodged in Rincewind's head as Discworld plunges towards a fiery red star that may spell doom for the entire planet. Lovecraftian influences are prominent in the early and late goings, although most of the book is a lighthearted slapstick parody of the fantasy genre. The story often appears direction</span>
  <span id="freeText15933844685800043322" style="display:none">Laurel and Hardy. Riggs and Murtaugh. Oscar and Felix. And continuing the grand tradition, the Discworld's own Rincewind and Twoflower. This time the story centers around the Octavo and the 8th spell lodged in Rincewind's head as Discworld plunges towards a fiery red star that may spell doom for the entire planet. Lovecraftian influences are prominent in the early and late goings, although most of the book is a lighthearted slapstick parody of the fantasy genre. The story often appears directionless and sags in the middle like an aging businessman but overall it's a quick and entertaining read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15933844685800043322" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15721056392339064249">Several of the other reviewers have singled out for special praise the Xena parody with the more appropriately dressed warrior princess. She was indeed very fine, but my personal favorite was the bit where the Stonehenge-type astronomical ritual unexpectedly develops a glitch. "Looks like software incompatibility!" says the know-it-all Neolithic geek. "The Spiral Chant doesn't work on concentric circles!"<br/><br/>And, while we're on rocks, I also loved the trolls, harking back to their glory days in earl</span>
  <span id="freeText15721056392339064249" style="display:none">Several of the other reviewers have singled out for special praise the Xena parody with the more appropriately dressed warrior princess. She was indeed very fine, but my personal favorite was the bit where the Stonehenge-type astronomical ritual unexpectedly develops a glitch. "Looks like software incompatibility!" says the know-it-all Neolithic geek. "The Spiral Chant doesn't work on concentric circles!"<br /><br />And, while we're on rocks, I also loved the trolls, harking back to their glory days in earlier geological eras. "Ah, back then you were igneous or nothing," one of them sighs. "But now, let's face it, we're all getting a bit metamorphic..."<br /><br />Yes... when you think about it, it must be rather frightening for a troll to realize that, oh my God, I'm already 500 million years old, where <i>did</i> all the time go?<br /></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer79886412" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4298362620248039619">If you read The Color of Magic, you most probably got this book as the the one preceding it (the aforementioned The Color of Magic) ended with Rincewind falling off the edge of the Discworld.... talk about a "cliff-hanger ending". In this one we'll go from there to what could be the end of the Discworld itself and possibly, well everything else. It all depends on Rincewind....scary thought that.<br/><br/>"Synopsisizers" (I believe I just made that word up, so bear with me, please) anyway, "the people who </span>
  <span id="freeText4298362620248039619" style="display:none">If you read The Color of Magic, you most probably got this book as the the one preceding it (the aforementioned The Color of Magic) ended with Rincewind falling off the edge of the Discworld.... talk about a "cliff-hanger ending". In this one we'll go from there to what could be the end of the Discworld itself and possibly, well everything else. It all depends on Rincewind....scary thought that.<br /><br />"Synopsisizers" (I believe I just made that word up, so bear with me, please) anyway, "the people who write synopses" love to say books (and for that matter movies, TV programs, songs, poems, and everthing else) are "irreverent". They think this will appeal to the rebel in each of us I suppose. In this case Pratchett's writings do tend to skewer "dogmas" but he does it pretty much across the board getting the irreligious as well as the religious. I'm a Christian and haven't found myself "outraged" to the point of hurling the book across the room or anything. I enjoy Sir Terry's work and while I'd probably disagree with him across the board on spiritual matters, I think I'd like him.<br /><br />I think that most anyone with an open mind (and maybe are sure what they themselves actually believe and realize that this is that arcane "thing" called "humor")can enjoy the Discworld books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4298362620248039619" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <i> The important thing about having lots of things to remember is that you've got to go somewhere afterwards where you can remember them, you see? You've got to stop. You haven't really been anywhere until you've got back home." </i>
</b><br /><br />The Discworld is a Disc sitting on the backs of four elephants, standing on the shell of a giant turtle that is slowly swimming it's way through Space...<br /><br />And as befits a world so ridiculous, it is filled with an array of equally ridiculous and loveable characters, including a piece of travelling Luggage with lots of tiny legs and an intimidating appetite. <span id="freeTextContainer15950688187332742778">This is not for me anymore. 15 years ago I read the first handful of Discworld books and liked them well enough. But even then this type of comedic writing wasn't really my cup of tea. Now it definitely isn't. Too little plot, too absurd. I laughed a few times, but the story did not engage me much.<br/><br/>My favourite scene was Death learning how how to play Bridge. The druids were fun. And the bits with the trolls. Cohen was a great character.<br/><br/>The idea behind the Discworld is a great one and I heard goo</span>
  <span id="freeText15950688187332742778" style="display:none">This is not for me anymore. 15 years ago I read the first handful of Discworld books and liked them well enough. But even then this type of comedic writing wasn't really my cup of tea. Now it definitely isn't. Too little plot, too absurd. I laughed a few times, but the story did not engage me much.<br /><br />My favourite scene was Death learning how how to play Bridge. The druids were fun. And the bits with the trolls. Cohen was a great character.<br /><br />The idea behind the Discworld is a great one and I heard good things about the later books. One of them is one my shelf and I will have a go at it later this year. Who knows, I might like it better.</span>

<div id="review_168812598" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/168812598" />
    <a title="Toby" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5454475-toby"><img alt="Toby" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1542247337p2/5454475.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/168812598?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Toby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Toby" href="/user/show/5454475-toby">Toby</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback " href="/book/show/601239.The_Light_Fantastic">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5454475-toby?shelf=funny">funny</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5454475-toby?shelf=fantastical">fantastical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer168812598" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13557961846393654767"><b>Unseen University but not as you know it.</b><br/><br/>With my awful and dreaded exercise regime continuing so too does my revisit to the early works of the Discworld thanks to the readings of Nigel Planer.<br/><br/>Rincewind, last seen falling off of the disc has been saved from certain death once more thanks to spoilers that won't be mentioned and now must save the disc from a fiery death and evil wizards.<br/><br/>The problem with going back to these early novels is that things arenlt as you remember them. It's like an altern</span>
  <span id="freeText13557961846393654767" style="display:none"><b>Unseen University but not as you know it.</b><br /><br />With my awful and dreaded exercise regime continuing so too does my revisit to the early works of the Discworld thanks to the readings of Nigel Planer.<br /><br />Rincewind, last seen falling off of the disc has been saved from certain death once more thanks to spoilers that won't be mentioned and now must save the disc from a fiery death and evil wizards.<br /><br />The problem with going back to these early novels is that things arenlt as you remember them. It's like an alternate universe where everything is the same only slightly different. Ridcully is beyond larger than life in the later novels and the supporting cast of wizards rounder, more interesting, so that this early incarnation of the internal politics of the wizards <b>feels a bit silly.</b> The same can be said for the trolls too. They're not the same entities from Thud for example.<br /><br />That aside this is <b>a jolly good romp</b> through fantasy cliches and a not so subtle critique of the weaknesses of the masses in the grip of fear. The pairing of Rincewind and Twoflower continue to grow dynamically and the development of the luggage as an actual character is fun to read. Added to the ensemble this time is the legendary hero Cohen The Barbarian and his virgin wife Bethan who provide an extra dimension of fun.<br /><br />Cohen and the trip to the Domain of Death stand out as high points for me and help this second book in the series to <b>surpass The Colour of Magic in terms of pleasure and entertainment.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="13557961846393654767" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1090827013" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1090827013" />
    <a title="Barry Pierce" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4593541-barry-pierce"><img alt="Barry Pierce" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588975731p2/4593541.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1090827013?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Barry Pierce" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Barry Pierce" href="/user/show/4593541-barry-pierce">Barry Pierce</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback " href="/book/show/601239.The_Light_Fantastic">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4593541-barry-pierce?shelf=20th-century">20th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4593541-barry-pierce?shelf=read-in-2014">read-in-2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1090827013" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1444927706606127852">This is reminded me of just how great Terry Pratchett is. His writing and humour is just fabulous and his characters are brilliant. However the plot of this novel is quite reminiscent of a wet tea towel. It doesn't hold a flame to <i>The Colour of Magic</i> and I'm quite glad that Pratchett gave up on the idea of doing sequels after this novel. It's overall very meh with a sprinkling of ugh. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('QyvMen3COfw948AOklK3ooNdTuVzmoCIEKF5LbX8ec55DaWoxpzwlJrIdG9lp719VQKpLb0XDu9L3z+ceL+LVA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('bxArXqVkIuwqeVqwEanzPoHkGUzOTgVGtXsXvuv0mANVNkKMHjrrhI1S7tHmXPnhV7v+hADDiyHuBVEPJrdqmQ==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3146170486358428093">Born Terence David John Pratchett, Sir Terry Pratchett sold his first story when he was thirteen, which earned him enough money to buy a second-hand typewriter. His first novel, a humorous fantasy entitled <i>The Carpet People</i>, appeared in 1971 from the publisher Colin Smythe. <br/><br/>Terry worked for many years as a journalist and press officer, writing in his spare time and publishing a number of novels, i</span>
  <span id="freeText3146170486358428093" style="display:none">Born Terence David John Pratchett, Sir Terry Pratchett sold his first story when he was thirteen, which earned him enough money to buy a second-hand typewriter. His first novel, a humorous fantasy entitled <i>The Carpet People</i>, appeared in 1971 from the publisher Colin Smythe. <br /><br />Terry worked for many years as a journalist and press officer, writing in his spare time and publishing a number of novels, including his first Discworld novel, <i>The Color of Magic</i>, in 1983. In 1987, he turned to writing full time. <br /><br />There are over 40 books in the Discworld series, of which four are written for children. The first of these, <i>The Amazing Maurice and His Educated Rodents</i>, won the Carnegie Medal. <br /><br />A non-Discworld book, <i>Good Omens</i>, his 1990 collaboration with Neil Gaiman, has been a longtime bestseller and was reissued in hardcover by William Morrow in early 2006 (it is also available as a mass market paperback - Harper Torch, 2006 - and trade paperback - Harper Paperbacks, 2006). <br /><br />In 2008, Harper Children's published Terry's standalone non-Discworld YA novel, <i>Nation</i>. Terry published <i>Snuff</i> in October 2011. <br /><br />Regarded as one of the most significant contemporary English-language satirists, Pratchett has won numerous literary awards, was named an Officer of the British Empire (OBE) “for services to literature” in 1998, and has received honorary doctorates from the University of Warwick in 1999, the University of Portsmouth in 2001, the University of Bath in 2003, the University of Bristol in 2004, Buckinghamshire New University in 2008, the University of Dublin in 2008, Bradford University in 2009, the University of Winchester in 2009, and The Open University in 2013 for his contribution to Public Service.<br /><br />In Dec. of 2007, Pratchett disclosed that he had been diagnosed with Alzheimer's disease. On 18 Feb, 2009, he was knighted by Queen Elizabeth II.<br /><br />He was awarded the World Fantasy Life Achievement Award in 2010.<br /><br />Sir Terry Pratchett passed away on 12th March 2015.</span>
